<p><b>Freddie Mercury</b> (5 September 1946 – 24 November 1991) was a British singer, songwriter and producer, best known as the <a href="/wiki/Lead_vocalist" title="Lead vocalist">lead vocalist</a> and lyricist of the rock band <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a>. As a performer, he was known for his flamboyant stage persona and powerful vocals over a four-<a href="/wiki/Octave" title="Octave">octave</a> range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> As a songwriter, he composed many hits for Queen, including "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Killer_Queen" title="Killer Queen">Killer Queen</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Somebody_to_Love_(Queen_song)" title="Somebody to Love (Queen song)">Somebody to Love</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Stop_Me_Now" title="Don't Stop Me Now">Don't Stop Me Now</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_Little_Thing_Called_Love" title="Crazy Little Thing Called Love">Crazy Little Thing Called Love</a>," and "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>." Mercury also led a solo career, and also occasionally served as a producer and guest musician (piano or vocals) for other artists.</p>
<p>Mercury was a <a href="/wiki/Parsi" title="Parsi">Parsi</a> born in the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Zanzibar" title="Sultanate of Zanzibar">Sultanate of Zanzibar</a> and grew up there and in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> until his mid-teens. He died of <a href="/wiki/Bronchopneumonia" title="Bronchopneumonia">bronchopneumonia</a> brought on by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS">AIDS</a> on 24 November 1991, one day after publicly acknowledging he had the disease. Posthumously, in 1992 he was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Award</a> for Outstanding Contribution to British Music, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury_Tribute_Concert" title="Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert">Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert</a> was held at Wembley Stadium, London. As a member of Queen, he was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> in 2001, the <a href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Songwriters Hall of Fame">Songwriters Hall of Fame</a> in 2003, the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="UK Music Hall of Fame">UK Music Hall of Fame</a> in 2004, and the band received a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> in 2002. Also in 2002, Mercury was placed at number 58 in the BBC's poll of the <a href="/wiki/100_Greatest_Britons" title="100 Greatest Britons">100 Greatest Britons</a>.</p>
<p>He has been voted one of the greatest singers in the history of popular music. In 2005, a poll organised by <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/MTV2" title="MTV2">MTV2</a> saw Mercury voted the best male singer of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2008, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> editors ranked him number 18 on their list of the 100 greatest singers ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, a <i><a href="/wiki/Classic_Rock_(magazine)" title="Classic Rock (magazine)">Classic Rock</a></i> poll elected him the best rock singer of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> has characterised Mercury as "one of rock's greatest all-time entertainers," who possessed "one of the greatest voices in all of music."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Mercury (born <b>Farrokh Bulsara</b>; <a href="/wiki/Gujarati_language" title="Gujarati language">Gujarati</a>: <i>ફારોખ બલસારા</i>, <i>Pharōkh Balsārā‌</i>) was born in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_protectorate" title="British protectorate">British protectorate</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Zanzibar" title="Sultanate of Zanzibar">Sultanate of Zanzibar</a>, East Africa (now part of <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mr-mercury.co.uk_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-mr-mercury.co.uk-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inourstar.com_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-inourstar.com-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> His parents, Bomi (1908–2003) and Jer Bulsara (1922–),<sup class="reference" id="ref_Bulsaranone"><a href="#endnote_Bulsaranone">[a]</a></sup> were <a href="/wiki/Parsi" title="Parsi">Parsis</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> region of the then province of <a href="/wiki/Bombay_Presidency" title="Bombay Presidency">Bombay Presidency</a> in <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LindaB_2000_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-LindaB_2000-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="ref_Parsisnone"><a href="#endnote_Parsisnone">[b]</a></sup> The family surname is derived from the town of Bulsar (now known as <a href="/wiki/Valsad" title="Valsad">Valsad</a>) in southern <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a>. As Parsis, Mercury and his family practised the <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrian</a> religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The Bulsara family had moved to <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Archipelago" title="Zanzibar Archipelago">Zanzibar</a> so that his father could continue his job as a cashier at the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Colonies" title="Secretary of State for the Colonies">British Colonial Office</a>. He had a younger sister, Kashmira.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Das_2000_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Das_2000-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Freddie_Mercury%27s_birthplace.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2094" data-file-width="1401" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Freddie_Mercury%27s_birthplace.jpg/170px-Freddie_Mercury%27s_birthplace.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Freddie_Mercury%27s_birthplace.jpg/255px-Freddie_Mercury%27s_birthplace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Freddie_Mercury%27s_birthplace.jpg/340px-Freddie_Mercury%27s_birthplace.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Freddie_Mercury%27s_birthplace.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The house in <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> where Mercury lived in his early years</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mercury spent most of his childhood in India and began taking piano lessons at the age of seven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1954, at the age of eight, Mercury was sent to study at <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Boys_School" title="St. Peter's Boys School">St. Peter's School</a>, a British-style boarding school for boys, in <a href="/wiki/Panchgani" title="Panchgani">Panchgani</a> near Bombay (now <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>), India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones_1998_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jones_1998-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> One of his formative musical influences at the time was <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Lata_Mangeshkar" title="Lata Mangeshkar">Lata Mangeshkar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> At the age of 12, he formed a school band, <a href="/wiki/The_Hectics" title="The Hectics">The Hectics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">covered</a> <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> artists such as <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Richard" title="Cliff Richard">Cliff Richard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Richard" title="Little Richard">Little Richard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hodkinson_2004_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hodkinson_2004-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> A friend from the time recalls that he had "an uncanny ability to listen to the radio and replay what he heard on piano."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Donnell_2005_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Donnell_2005-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also at St. Peter's where he began to call himself "Freddie", and in February 1963 he moved back to Zanzibar where he joined his parents at their flat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At the age of 17, Mercury and his family fled from Zanzibar for safety reasons due to the 1964 <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Revolution" title="Zanzibar Revolution">Zanzibar Revolution</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Januszczak_1996_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Januszczak_1996-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> in which thousands of Arabs and Indians were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The family moved into a small house in <a href="/wiki/Feltham" title="Feltham">Feltham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middlesex" title="Middlesex">Middlesex</a>, England. Mercury enrolled at <a href="/wiki/Isleworth" title="Isleworth">Isleworth</a> Polytechnic (now <a href="/wiki/West_Thames_College" title="West Thames College">West Thames College</a>) in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_(London_sub_region)" title="West (London sub region)">West London</a> where he studied art. He ultimately earned a diploma in Art and Graphic Design at <a href="/wiki/Ealing_Art_College" title="Ealing Art College">Ealing Art College</a> (now the Ealing campus of <a href="/wiki/University_of_West_London" title="University of West London">University of West London</a>), later using these skills to design the Queen crest. A British citizen at birth, Mercury remained so for the rest of his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones_1998_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jones_1998-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following graduation, Mercury joined a series of bands and sold second-hand clothes in the <a href="/wiki/Kensington_Market,_London" title="Kensington Market, London">Kensington Market</a> in London with girlfriend Mary Austin. He also held a job at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a>. Friends from the time remember him as a quiet and shy young man who showed a great deal of interest in music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-student_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-student-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1969 he joined the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> based band, <a href="/wiki/Ibex_(band)" title="Ibex (band)">Ibex</a>, later renamed Wreckage. He lived briefly in a flat above the Liverpool pub, The Dovedale Towers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> When this band failed to take off, he joined a second band called <a href="/wiki/Sour_Milk_Sea_(band)" title="Sour Milk Sea (band)">Sour Milk Sea</a>. However, by early 1970 this group had broken up as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skala_2006_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Skala_2006-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In April 1970 Mercury joined guitarist <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a> and drummer <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taylor_(Queen_drummer)" title="Roger Taylor (Queen drummer)">Roger Taylor</a> who had previously been in a band called <a href="/wiki/Smile_(band)" title="Smile (band)">Smile</a>. Despite reservations of the other members and <a href="/wiki/Trident_Studios" title="Trident Studios">Trident Studios</a>, the band's initial management, Mercury chose the name "Queen" for the new band. He later said, "I was certainly aware of the gay connotations, but that was just one facet of it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Highleyman_2005_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Highleyman_2005-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> At about the same time, he changed his surname, Bulsara, to Mercury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singer">Singer</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FreddieMercurySinging1977.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="336" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/FreddieMercurySinging1977.jpg/180px-FreddieMercurySinging1977.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/FreddieMercurySinging1977.jpg/270px-FreddieMercurySinging1977.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/FreddieMercurySinging1977.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FreddieMercurySinging1977.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Freddie Mercury in 1978</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Freddie_Mercury_range_(F2-F6,_with_falsetto).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="550" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Freddie_Mercury_range_%28F2-F6%2C_with_falsetto%29.svg/130px-Freddie_Mercury_range_%28F2-F6%2C_with_falsetto%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Freddie_Mercury_range_%28F2-F6%2C_with_falsetto%29.svg/195px-Freddie_Mercury_range_%28F2-F6%2C_with_falsetto%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Freddie_Mercury_range_%28F2-F6%2C_with_falsetto%29.svg/260px-Freddie_Mercury_range_%28F2-F6%2C_with_falsetto%29.svg.png 2x" width="130"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Freddie_Mercury_range_(F2-F6,_with_falsetto).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mercury's vocal range</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although Mercury's speaking <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voice" title="Voice">voice</a> naturally fell in the <a href="/wiki/Baritone" title="Baritone">baritone</a> range, he delivered most songs in the <a href="/wiki/Tenor" title="Tenor">tenor</a> range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> His vocal range extended from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bass_(voice)" title="Bass (voice)">bass</a> low F (<a href="/wiki/Scientific_pitch_notation" title="Scientific pitch notation">F2</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Soprano" title="Soprano">soprano</a> high F (F6).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soto_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-soto-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> He could <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belt_(music)" title="Belt (music)">belt</a> up to <a href="/wiki/Tenor" title="Tenor">tenor</a> high F (F5).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soto_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-soto-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Biographer <a href="/wiki/David_Bret" title="David Bret">David Bret</a> described his voice as "escalating within a few bars from a deep, throaty rock-growl to tender, vibrant tenor, then on to a high-pitched, perfect <a href="/wiki/Coloratura" title="Coloratura">coloratura</a>, pure and crystalline in the upper reaches."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bret_1996_26_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bret_1996_26-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Spanish <a href="/wiki/Soprano" title="Soprano">soprano</a> <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Caball%C3%A9" title="Montserrat Caballé">Montserrat Caballé</a>, with whom Mercury recorded an album, expressed her opinion that "the difference between Freddie and almost all the other rock stars was that he was selling the voice."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cain_2006_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cain_2006-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> She adds,</p>
<blockquote>
<p>His technique was astonishing. No problem of <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">tempo</a>, he sung with an incisive sense of rhythm, his vocal placement was very good and he was able to glide effortlessly from a register to another. He also had a great musicality. His phrasing was subtle, delicate and sweet or energetic and slamming. He was able to find the right colouring or expressive nuance for each word.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-soto_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-soto-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>As Queen's career progressed, he would increasingly alter the highest notes of their songs when live, often harmonising with seconds, thirds or fifths instead. Mercury was said to have "the rawest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vocal_fold_nodules" title="Vocal fold nodules">vocal fold nodules</a>" and claimed never to have had any formal vocal training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rush2_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rush2-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Songwriter">Songwriter</span></h3>
<p>Mercury wrote 10 of the 17 songs on Queen's <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Queen_album)" title="Greatest Hits (Queen album)">Greatest Hits</a></i> album: "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Seven_Seas_of_Rhye" title="Seven Seas of Rhye">Seven Seas of Rhye</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Killer_Queen" title="Killer Queen">Killer Queen</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Somebody_to_Love_(Queen_song)" title="Somebody to Love (Queen song)">Somebody to Love</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Good_Old-Fashioned_Lover_Boy" title="Good Old-Fashioned Lover Boy">Good Old-Fashioned Lover Boy</a>," "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Bicycle_Race" title="Bicycle Race">Bicycle Race</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Stop_Me_Now" title="Don't Stop Me Now">Don't Stop Me Now</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_Little_Thing_Called_Love" title="Crazy Little Thing Called Love">Crazy Little Thing Called Love</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Play_the_Game_(song)" title="Play the Game (song)">Play the Game</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The most notable aspect of his songwriting involved the wide range of genres that he used, which included, among other styles, <a href="/wiki/Rockabilly" title="Rockabilly">rockabilly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gospel_music" title="Gospel music">gospel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">disco</a>. As he explained in a 1986 interview, "I hate doing the same thing again and again and again. I like to see what's happening now in music, film and theatre and incorporate all of those things."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wenner_2001_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wenner_2001-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Compared to many popular songwriters, Mercury also tended to write musically complex material. For example, "Bohemian Rhapsody" is acyclic in structure and comprises dozens of <a href="/wiki/Chord_(music)" title="Chord (music)">chords</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_1992_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_1992-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aledort_2003_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aledort_2003-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> He also wrote six songs from <i><a href="/wiki/Queen_II" title="Queen II">Queen II</a></i> which deal with multiple key changes and complex material. "Crazy Little Thing Called Love," on the other hand, contains only a few chords. Despite the fact that Mercury often wrote very intricate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harmonies" title="Harmonies">harmonies</a>, he also claimed that he could barely read music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coleman_1981_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coleman_1981-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> He wrote most of his songs on the piano and used a wide variety of different key signatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Queen_1992_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Queen_1992-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performer">Live performer</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:174px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_1984_0009.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="196" height="374" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Queen_1984_0009.jpg/172px-Queen_1984_0009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/Queen_1984_0009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/Queen_1984_0009.jpg 2x" width="172"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_1984_0009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mercury performing live in September 1984</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mercury was noted for his live performances, which were often delivered to stadium audiences around the world. He displayed a highly theatrical style that often evoked a great deal of participation from the crowd. A writer for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spectator" title="The Spectator">The Spectator</a></i> described him as "a performer out to tease, shock and ultimately charm his audience with various extravagant versions of himself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blaikie_1996_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Blaikie_1996-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>, who performed at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freddie_Mercury_Tribute_Concert" title="Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert">Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert</a> and recorded the song "<a href="/wiki/Under_Pressure" title="Under Pressure">Under Pressure</a>" with Queen, praised Mercury's performance style, saying: "Of all the more theatrical rock performers, Freddie took it further than the rest... he took it over the edge. And of course, I always admired a man who wears tights. I only saw him in concert once and as they say, he was definitely a man who could hold an audience in the palm of his hand."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ressner_1992_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner_1992-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Queen guitarist Brian May wrote that Mercury could make "the last person at the back of the furthest stand in a stadium feel that he was connected."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>One of Mercury's most notable performances with Queen took place at <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> in 1985, during which the entire stadium audience of 72,000 people clapped, sang and swayed in unison. Queen's performance at the event has since been voted by a group of music executives as the greatest live performance in the history of rock music. The results were aired on a television program called "The World's Greatest Gigs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Minchin_2005_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Minchin_2005-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2005b_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2005b-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> In reviewing Live Aid in 2005, one critic wrote, "Those who compile lists of Great Rock Frontmen and award the top spots to <a href="/wiki/Mick_Jagger" title="Mick Jagger">Mick Jagger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Plant" title="Robert Plant">Robert Plant</a>, etc all are guilty of a terrible oversight. Freddie, as evidenced by his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dionysian" title="Dionysian">Dionysian</a> Live Aid performance, was easily the most godlike of them all."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harris_2005_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harris_2005-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Over the course of his career, Mercury performed an estimated 700 concerts in countries around the world with Queen. A notable aspect of Queen concerts was the large scale involved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wenner_2001_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wenner_2001-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> He once explained, "We're the <a href="/wiki/Cecil_B._DeMille" title="Cecil B. DeMille">Cecil B. DeMille</a> of rock and roll, always wanting to do things bigger and better."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wenner_2001_32-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wenner_2001-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The band was the first ever to play in South American stadiums, breaking worldwide records for concert attendance in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morumbi_Stadium" title="Morumbi Stadium">Morumbi Stadium</a> in São Paulo in 1981.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bret_1996_91_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bret_1996_91-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1986, Queen also played behind the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> when they performed to a crowd of 80,000 in <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, in what was one of the biggest rock concerts ever held in Eastern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Mercury's final live performance with Queen took place on 9 August 1986 at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Knebworth_Park" title="Knebworth Park">Knebworth Park</a> in England and drew an attendance estimated as high as 160,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-knebworth_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-knebworth-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> With the British national anthem "<a href="/wiki/God_Save_the_Queen" title="God Save the Queen">God Save the Queen</a>" playing at the end of the concert, Mercury's final act on stage saw him draped in a robe, holding a golden crown aloft, bidding farewell to the crowd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Instrumentalist">Instrumentalist</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_1984_012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="522" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Queen_1984_012.jpg/180px-Queen_1984_012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Queen_1984_012.jpg/270px-Queen_1984_012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Queen_1984_012.jpg/360px-Queen_1984_012.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_1984_012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mercury playing guitar during a live concert with Queen in Frankfurt, Germany, 1984.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As a young boy in India, Mercury received formal piano training up to the age of nine. Later on, while living in London, he learned guitar. Much of the music he liked was guitar-oriented: his favourite artists at the time were <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">The Who</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>. He was often self-deprecating about his own skills on both instruments and from the early 1980s onward began extensively using guest keyboardists for both Queen and his solo career. Most notably, he enlisted <a href="/wiki/Fred_Mandel" title="Fred Mandel">Fred Mandel</a> (a Canadian musician who also worked for <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> and <a href="/wiki/Supertramp" title="Supertramp">Supertramp</a>) for his first solo project, and from 1985 onward collaborated with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mike_Moran_(music_producer)" title="Mike Moran (music producer)">Mike Moran</a> (in the studio) and <a href="/wiki/Spike_Edney" title="Spike Edney">Spike Edney</a> (in concert), leaving most of the keyboard work exclusively to them.</p>
<p>Mercury played the piano in many of Queen's most popular songs, including "<a href="/wiki/Killer_Queen" title="Killer Queen">Killer Queen</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>," "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Good_Old_Fashioned_Lover_Boy" title="Good Old Fashioned Lover Boy">Good Old Fashioned Lover Boy</a>," "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Somebody_to_Love_(Queen_song)" title="Somebody to Love (Queen song)">Somebody To Love</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Stop_Me_Now" title="Don't Stop Me Now">Don't Stop Me Now</a>." He used concert <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_piano" title="Grand piano">grand pianos</a> and, occasionally, other keyboard instruments such as the <a href="/wiki/Harpsichord" title="Harpsichord">harpsichord</a>. From 1980 onward, he also made frequent use of synthesisers in the studio. Queen guitarist <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a> claims that Mercury was unimpressed with his own abilities at the piano and used the instrument less over time because he wanted to walk around onstage and entertain the audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Longfellow_2006_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Longfellow_2006-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Although he wrote many lines for the guitar, Mercury possessed only rudimentary skills on the instrument. Songs like "<a href="/wiki/Ogre_Battle_(song)" title="Ogre Battle (song)">Ogre Battle</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Crazy_Little_Thing_Called_Love" title="Crazy Little Thing Called Love">Crazy Little Thing Called Love</a>" were composed on the guitar; the latter featured Mercury playing <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_guitar" title="Acoustic guitar">acoustic guitar</a> both onstage and in the studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solo_career">Solo career</span></h3>
<p>In addition to his work with Queen, Mercury put out two solo albums and several singles. Although his solo work was not as commercially successful as most Queen albums, the two off-Queen albums and several of the singles debuted in the top 10 of the <a href="/wiki/UK_Music_Charts" title="UK Music Charts">UK Music Charts</a>. His first solo effort involved his contribution to the <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wolf" title="Richard Wolf">Richard "Wolfie" Wolf</a> mix of <i>Love Kills</i> on the 1984 album (the song also used as the end title theme for National Lampoon's "Loaded Weapon") and new soundtrack to the 1927 <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Lang" title="Fritz Lang">Fritz Lang</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Metropolis_(1927_film)" title="Metropolis (1927 film)">Metropolis</a></i>. The song, produced by <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Moroder" title="Giorgio Moroder">Giorgio Moroder</a>, debuted at the number 10 position in the UK charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReesCrampton_1999_809_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReesCrampton_1999_809-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Mercury's two full albums outside the band were <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Bad_Guy" title="Mr. Bad Guy">Mr. Bad Guy</a></i> (1985) and <i><a href="/wiki/Barcelona_(album)" title="Barcelona (album)">Barcelona</a></i> (1988). <i>Mr. Bad Guy</i> debuted in the top ten of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Album_Charts" title="UK Album Charts">UK Album Charts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReesCrampton_1999_809_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReesCrampton_1999_809-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1993, a remix of "<a href="/wiki/Living_on_My_Own" title="Living on My Own">Living on My Own</a>," a single from the album, reached the No. 1 position on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Charts" title="UK Singles Charts">UK Singles Charts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReesCrampton_1999_811_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReesCrampton_1999_811-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> The song also garnered Mercury a posthumous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Award" title="Ivor Novello Award">Ivor Novello Award</a>. Allmusic critic Eduardo Rivadavia describes <i>Mr. Bad Guy</i> as "outstanding from start to finish" and expressed his view that Mercury "did a commendable job of stretching into uncharted territory."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rivadavia_notdated_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rivadavia_notdated-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> In particular, the album is heavily synthesiser-driven in a way that is not characteristic of previous Queen albums.</p>
<p>His second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Barcelona_(album)" title="Barcelona (album)">Barcelona</a></i>, recorded with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spanish</a> <a href="/wiki/Soprano" title="Soprano">soprano</a> <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Caball%C3%A9" title="Montserrat Caballé">Montserrat Caballé</a>, combines elements of popular music and opera. Many critics were uncertain what to make of the album; one referred to it as "the most bizarre CD of the year."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bradley_1992_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bradley_1992-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was a commercial success,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barcelona_(Freddie_Mercury_song)" title="Barcelona (Freddie Mercury song)">album's title track</a> debuted at the No. 8 position in the UK charts and was a hit in Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReesCrampton_1999_810_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReesCrampton_1999_810-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> The title track received massive air play as the official anthem of the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Summer Olympics</a> (held in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> one year after Mercury's death). Caballé sang it live at the opening of the Olympics with Mercury's part played on a screen, and again prior to the start of the <a href="/wiki/1999_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1999 UEFA Champions League Final">1999 UEFA Champions League Final</a> in Barcelona.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to the two solo albums, Mercury released several singles, including his own version of the hit <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Pretender" title="The Great Pretender">The Great Pretender</a> by <a href="/wiki/The_Platters" title="The Platters">The Platters</a>, which debuted at No. 5 in the UK in 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReesCrampton_1999_809_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-ReesCrampton_1999_809-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2006 a compilation album featuring Mercury's solo work was released in the UK in honour of what would have been his 60th birthday. The album debuted in the top 10 of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Album_Charts" title="UK Album Charts">UK Album Charts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1981–1983 Mercury recorded several tracks with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, including a demo of "<a href="/wiki/State_of_Shock_(song)" title="State of Shock (song)">State of Shock</a>," "Victory" and "There Must Be More to Life Than This."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> None of these collaborations were officially released, although <a href="/wiki/Bootleg_recording" title="Bootleg recording">bootleg</a> recordings exist. Jackson went on to record the single "State of Shock" with <a href="/wiki/Mick_Jagger" title="Mick Jagger">Mick Jagger</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Jacksons" title="The Jacksons">The Jacksons</a>' album <i><a href="/wiki/Victory_(The_Jacksons_album)" title="Victory (The Jacksons album)">Victory</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Mercury included the solo version of "There Must Be More To Life Than This" on his <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Bad_Guy" title="Mr. Bad Guy">Mr. Bad Guy</a></i> album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2011, Brian May announced that a series of duets that Mercury recorded with Jackson were to be released in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> He later updated the release date to autumn of 2013 and then to 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RS_20130729_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-RS_20130729-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to working with Michael Jackson, Mercury and <a href="/wiki/Roger_Taylor_(Queen_drummer)" title="Roger Taylor (Queen drummer)">Roger Taylor</a> sang on the title track for <a href="/wiki/Billy_Squier" title="Billy Squier">Billy Squier</a>'s 1982 studio release, <i><a href="/wiki/Emotions_in_Motion" title="Emotions in Motion">Emotions in Motion</a></i> and later contributed to two tracks on Squier's 1986 release, <i><a href="/wiki/Enough_Is_Enough_(album)" title="Enough Is Enough (album)">Enough Is Enough</a></i>, providing vocals on "Love is the Hero" and musical arrangements on "Lady With a Tenor Sax".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships">Relationships</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Freddie_house.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3968" data-file-width="2232" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Freddie_house.JPG/180px-Freddie_house.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Freddie_house.JPG/270px-Freddie_house.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Freddie_house.JPG/360px-Freddie_house.JPG 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Freddie_house.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mercury lived at 12 Stafford Terrace in <a href="/wiki/Kensington" title="Kensington">Kensington</a>, London, before moving into Garden Lodge</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the early 1970s Mercury had a long-term relationship with Mary Austin, whom he had met through guitarist <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a>. He lived with Austin for several years in <a href="/wiki/West_Kensington" title="West Kensington">West Kensington</a>, London. By the mid-1970s, the singer had begun an affair with a male American record executive at <a href="/wiki/Elektra_Records" title="Elektra Records">Elektra Records</a> and, in December 1976, Mercury told Austin of his sexuality, which ended their romantic relationship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Teckman_2004_part2_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Teckman_2004_part2-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LesleyJones_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-LesleyJones-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Mercury moved out of the flat they shared together and into 12 Stafford Terrace in Kensington and bought Austin a place of her own nearby.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LesleyJones_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-LesleyJones-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> They remained close friends through the years, with Mercury often referring to her as his only true friend. In a 1985 interview, Mercury said of Austin, "All my lovers asked me why they couldn't replace Mary [Austin], but it's simply impossible. The only friend I've got is Mary and I don't want anybody else. To me, she was my common-law wife. To me, it was a marriage. We believe in each other, that's enough for me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hauptfuhrer_1977_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hauptfuhrer_1977-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> He also wrote several songs about Austin, the most notable of which is "<a href="/wiki/Love_of_My_Life_(Queen_song)" title="Love of My Life (Queen song)">Love of My Life</a>." Mercury's final home, Garden Lodge, 1 <a href="/wiki/Logan_Place" title="Logan Place">Logan Place</a>, a twenty-eight room <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Georgian</a> mansion in Kensington set in a quarter-acre manicured garden surrounded by a high brick wall, had been picked out by Austin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> In his will, Mercury left his London home to Austin, rather than his then partner Jim Hutton, saying to her, "You would have been my wife and it would have been yours anyway."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Mercury was also the godfather of Mary's oldest son, Richard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Longfellow_2006_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Longfellow_2006-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the early to mid '80s, he was romantically involved with <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Valentin" title="Barbara Valentin">Barbara Valentin</a>, an Austrian actress,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> who is featured in the video for "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Hard_Life" title="It's a Hard Life">It's a Hard Life</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1985, he began another long-term relationship with hairdresser Jim Hutton (1949–2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Hutton, who was tested HIV-positive in 1990,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hutton_1994_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hutton_1994-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> lived with Mercury for the last six years of his life, nursed him during his illness and was present at his bedside when he died. Hutton said Mercury died wearing the wedding band that Hutton had given him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hutton_1994_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hutton_1994-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Friendship_with_Kenny_Everett">Friendship with Kenny Everett</span></h3>
<p>Radio DJ <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Everett" title="Kenny Everett">Kenny Everett</a> first met Mercury in 1974 when he invited the singer on to his breakfast show on <a href="/wiki/Capital_London" title="Capital London">Capital London</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Everett_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Everett-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> As two of Britain's most flamboyant, outrageous and best-loved entertainers, they shared much in common and instantly became close friends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Everett_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Everett-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Everett would play a major role in Queen's early success, when, in 1975, armed with an advanced copy of the single "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>", Mercury went to see Everett.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> While privately Everett doubted any station would play the song due to its length at over 6 minutes, he said nothing to Mercury and placed the song on the turntable, and after hearing it he enthused: "forget it, it's going to be number one for centuries."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_66-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> While Capital Radio hadn't officially accepted the song, the anarchic Everett would talk incessantly about a record he had but couldn't play, before the song "accidentally" started playing, with Everett stating: "Oops, my finger must've slipped."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_66-3"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Capital's switchboard was jammed with callers wanting to know when the song was going to be released – on one occasion Everett aired the song 36 times in one day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Everett_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-Everett-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1970s, their friendship became closer, with Everett becoming advisor and mentor to Mercury, and Mercury as Everett's confidante, helping him to accept his sexuality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Everett_72-3"><a href="#cite_note-Everett-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Throughout the early-mid 80s, they continued to explore their homosexuality, as well as experimenting in drugs, and although they were never lovers, they did experience London night life on a regular basis together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Everett_72-4"><a href="#cite_note-Everett-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> By 1985, they had fallen out over a disagreement on their using and sharing of drugs, and their friendship was further strained when Everett was outed by his biographer Audrey Lee "Lady Lee" Middleton, with Mercury taking Lee's side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Everett_72-5"><a href="#cite_note-Everett-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> With both suffering from failing health, Mercury and Everett started talking again in 1989, and they were able to reconcile their differences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Everett_72-6"><a href="#cite_note-Everett-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sexual_orientation">Sexual orientation</span></h3>
<p>While some commentators claimed Mercury hid his sexual orientation from the public,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Januszczak_1996_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Januszczak_1996-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cain_2006_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cain_2006-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Landesman_2006_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Landesman_2006-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> others claimed he was "openly gay."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fitzpatrick_2006_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzpatrick_2006-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2006_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2006-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 1974, when asked directly, "So how about being bent?" by the <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">New Musical Express</a></i>, Mercury replied, "You're a crafty cow. Let's put it this way; there were times when I was young and green. It's a thing schoolboys go through. I've had my share of schoolboy pranks. I'm not going to elaborate further." Homosexual acts between adult males over the age of 21 were decriminalised in the United Kingdom in 1967, only seven years earlier. In the 1980s, he would often distance himself from his partner, Jim Hutton, during public events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hutton_1994_71-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hutton_1994-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 1986, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> claimed Mercury had "confessed to a string of one-night gay sex affairs."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Sun_October_1986_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Sun_October_1986-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During his career, Mercury's flamboyant stage performances sometimes led journalists to allude to his sexuality. Dave Dickson, reviewing Queen's performance at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Arena" title="Wembley Arena">Wembley Arena</a> in 1984 for <i><a href="/wiki/Kerrang!" title="Kerrang!">Kerrang!</a></i>, noted Mercury's "camp" addresses to the audience and even described him as a "posing, pouting, posturing tart."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1992, John Marshall of <i><a href="/wiki/Gay_Times" title="Gay Times">Gay Times</a></i> expressed the following opinion: "[Mercury] was a 'scene-queen,' not afraid to publicly express his gayness, but unwilling to analyse or justify his 'lifestyle' ... It was as if Freddie Mercury was saying to the world, 'I am what I am. So what?' And that in itself for some was a statement."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leung_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leung-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> In an article for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AfterElton" title="AfterElton">AfterElton</a></i>, Robert Urban stated: "Mercury did not ally himself to 'political <a href="/wiki/Coming_out" title="Coming out">outness</a>,' or to <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">GLBT</a> causes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leung_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-Leung-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personality">Personality</span></h3>
<p>Although he cultivated a flamboyant stage personality, Mercury was shy and retiring when not performing, particularly around people he did not know well,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O.27Donnell_2005_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Donnell_2005-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cain_2006_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cain_2006-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> and granted very few interviews. Mercury once said of himself: "When I'm performing I'm an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extrovert" title="Extrovert">extrovert</a>, yet inside I'm a completely different man."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Myers_1991_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Myers_1991-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> While on stage, Mercury basked in the love from his audience; <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain" title="Kurt Cobain">Kurt Cobain</a>'s suicide note mentions how he both admired and envied the way Mercury "seemed to love, relish in the love and adoration from the crowd."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSBestSingers_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-RSBestSingers-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1987 Mercury celebrated his 41st birthday at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pikes_Hotel,_Ibiza" title="Pikes Hotel, Ibiza">Pikes Hotel, Ibiza</a>, several months after discovering that he had contracted <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson2011_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson2011-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> Mercury sought much comfort at the retreat and was a close friend of the owner, Anthony Pike, who described Mercury as "the most beautiful person I've ever met in my life. So entertaining and generous."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TI0802_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-TI0802-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> According to biographer <a href="/wiki/Lesley-Ann_Jones" title="Lesley-Ann Jones">Lesley-Ann Jones</a>, Mercury "felt very much at home there. He played some tennis, lounged by the pool, and ventured out to the odd gay club or bar at night."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones2011_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jones2011-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The party, held on 5 September 1987, has been described as "the most incredible example of excess the Mediterranean island had ever seen," and was attended by some 700 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TP96_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-TP96-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> A cake in the shape of Gaudi's <a href="/wiki/Sagrada_Fam%C3%ADlia" title="Sagrada Família">Sagrada Família</a> was provided for the party, although the original cake collapsed and was replaced with a 2 metre-long sponge with the notes from Mercury's song "Barcelona."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TI0802_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-TI0802-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> The bill, which included 232 broken glasses, was presented to Queen's manager, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Beach" title="Jim Beach">Jim Beach</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Illness_and_death">Illness and death</span></h2>
<p>In October 1986 the British press reported that Mercury had his blood tested for HIV/AIDS at a <a href="/wiki/Harley_Street" title="Harley Street">Harley Street</a> clinic. A reporter for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Whittow" title="Hugh Whittow">Hugh Whittow</a>, questioned Mercury about the story at Heathrow Airport as he was returning from a trip to Japan. Mercury denied he had a sexually transmitted disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Sun_October_1986_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Sun_October_1986-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> According to his partner Jim Hutton, Mercury was diagnosed with AIDS shortly after Easter of 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Teeman_2006_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Teeman_2006-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Around that time, Mercury claimed in an interview to have tested negative for HIV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cain_2006_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-Cain_2006-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite the denials, the British press pursued the rampant rumours over the next few years, fuelled by Mercury's increasingly gaunt appearance, Queen's absence from touring and reports from former lovers to various tabloid journals – by 1990 the rumours about Mercury's health were rife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bret_1996_138_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bret_1996_138-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_BRIT_Awards_ceremonies#1990" title="List of BRIT Awards ceremonies">1990</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brit_Award" title="Brit Award">Brit Awards</a> held at the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_Theatre" title="Dominion Theatre">Dominion Theatre</a>, London on 18 February, a visibly frail Mercury made his final public appearance on stage when he joined the rest of Queen to collect the Brit Award for Outstanding Contribution to Music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Towards the end of his life, he was routinely stalked by photographers, while the daily tabloid newspaper, <i>The Sun</i>, featured a series of articles claiming that he was seriously ill; notably in an article from November 1990 that featured an image of a haggard-looking Mercury on the front page accompanied by the headline, "It's official – Freddie is seriously ill."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_1997_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson_1997-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>However, Mercury and his inner circle of colleagues and friends, whom he felt he could trust, continually denied the stories, even after one front page article published on 29 April 1991 that showed Mercury appearing very haggard in what was by then a rare public appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> It has been suggested that he could have made a contribution to AIDS awareness by speaking earlier about his situation and his fight against the disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sky_1992_163_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sky_1992_163-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Mercury kept his condition private to protect those closest to him, with Brian May confirming in a 1993 interview he had informed the band of his illness much earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bret_1996_179_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bret_1996_179-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> Filmed in May 1991, the <a href="/wiki/These_Are_the_Days_of_Our_Lives#Music_video" title="These Are the Days of Our Lives">music video</a> for "<a href="/wiki/These_Are_the_Days_of_Our_Lives" title="These Are the Days of Our Lives">These Are the Days of Our Lives</a>" features a very thin Mercury, in what are his final scenes in front of the camera.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After the conclusion of his work with Queen in June 1991 Mercury retired to his home in <a href="/wiki/Kensington" title="Kensington">Kensington</a>. His former partner, Mary Austin, had been a particular comfort in his final years, and in the last few weeks of his life made regular visits to his home to look after him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Austin_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Austin-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Near the end of his life Mercury was starting to lose his sight and his deterioration was so overpowering he could not get out of bed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Austin_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-Austin-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Due to his worsening condition, Mercury decided to hasten his death by refusing to take his medication and continued taking only pain killers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Austin_99-2"><a href="#cite_note-Austin-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 November 1991 Mercury called Queen's manager Jim Beach over to his Kensington home to discuss a public statement. The next day the following announcement was made to the international press on behalf of Mercury:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bret_1996_179_96-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bret_1996_179-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Following the enormous conjecture in the press over the last two weeks, I wish to confirm that I have been tested HIV positive and have AIDS. I felt it correct to keep this information private to date to protect the privacy of those around me. However, the time has come now for my friends and fans around the world to know the truth and I hope that everyone will join with me, my doctors and all those worldwide in the fight against this terrible disease. My privacy has always been very special to me and I am famous for my lack of interviews. Please understand this policy will continue.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>On the evening of 24 November 1991, a little over 24 hours after issuing that statement, Mercury died at the age of 45 at his home in Kensington.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-otd_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-otd-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> The official cause of death was <a href="/wiki/Bronchopneumonia" title="Bronchopneumonia">bronchial pneumonia</a> resulting from AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Biochannel_2007_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Biochannel_2007-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> Mercury's close friend, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Clark_(musician)" title="Dave Clark (musician)">Dave Clark</a> of the <a href="/wiki/The_Dave_Clark_Five" title="The Dave Clark Five">The Dave Clark Five</a>, had taken over the bedside vigil when he died. Austin phoned Mercury's parents and sister to break the news of his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The news of his death reached newspaper and television crews by the early hours of 25 November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 November, Mercury's funeral service was conducted by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoroastrian" title="Zoroastrian">Zoroastrian</a> priest. An intensely private man, Mercury's service was for 35 of his close friends and family, with the remaining members of Queen and <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> among those in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Mercury was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cremated" title="Cremated">cremated</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kensal_Green_Cemetery" title="Kensal Green Cemetery">Kensal Green Cemetery</a>, West London. In accordance with Mercury's wishes, Mary Austin took possession of his ashes and buried them in an undisclosed location. The whereabouts of his ashes are believed to be known only to Mary Austin, who has stated that she will never reveal where she buried them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Freddie_Mercury_house.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Freddie_Mercury_house.jpg/220px-Freddie_Mercury_house.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Freddie_Mercury_house.jpg/330px-Freddie_Mercury_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Freddie_Mercury_house.jpg/440px-Freddie_Mercury_house.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Freddie_Mercury_house.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The outer walls of Garden Lodge, 1 <a href="/wiki/Logan_Place" title="Logan Place">Logan Place</a> became a shrine to Mercury. Pictured in 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In his will, Mercury left the vast majority of his wealth, including his home and recording royalties, to Mary Austin and the remainder to his parents and sister. He left £500,000 to his chef, Joe Fanelli, £500,000 to his personal assistant, Peter Freestone, £100,000 to his driver, Terry Giddings and £500,000 to Jim Hutton.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wigg_2000_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wigg_2000-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> Mary Austin continues to live at Mercury's former home, Garden Lodge, Kensington, with her family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wigg_2000_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wigg_2000-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The outer walls of Garden Lodge in 1 <a href="/wiki/Logan_Place" title="Logan Place">Logan Place</a> became a shrine to Mercury following his death, with mourners paying tribute by covering the walls in graffiti messages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Womack_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Womack-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Three years after his death, <i>Time Out</i> magazine reported, "Since Freddie's death, the wall outside the house has become London's biggest rock 'n' roll shrine."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Womack_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-Womack-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Today fans continue to visit to pay their respects with messages in letters appearing on the walls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Hutton was involved in a 2000 biography of Mercury, <i>Freddie Mercury, the Untold Story</i> and also gave an interview for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> for what would have been Mercury's 60th birthday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Teeman_2006_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-Teeman_2006-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_popularity">Continued popularity</span></h3>
<p>The extent to which Mercury's death may have enhanced Queen's popularity is not clear. In the United States, where Queen's popularity had lagged in the 1980s, sales of Queen albums went up dramatically in 1992, the year following his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_2007_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA_2007-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1992 one American critic noted, "What cynics call the 'dead star' factor had come into play—Queen is in the middle of a major resurgence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_1992_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_1992-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> The movie <i><a href="/wiki/Wayne%27s_World_(film)" title="Wayne's World (film)">Wayne's World</a></i>, which featured "Bohemian Rhapsody," also came out in 1992. According to the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a>, Queen has sold 34.5 million albums in the United States, about half of which have been sold since Mercury's death in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Estimates of Queen's total worldwide record sales to date have been set as high as 300 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cota_2006_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cota_2006-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> In the UK, Queen has now spent more collective weeks on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_Album_Charts" title="UK Album Charts">UK Album Charts</a> than any other musical act (including <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_2005a_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_2005a-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i>Queen's Greatest Hits</i> is the highest selling album of all time in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_2006_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown_2006-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Two of Mercury's songs, "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>," have also each been voted as the greatest song of all time in major polls by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sony_Ericsson" title="Sony Ericsson">Sony Ericsson</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haines_2005_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haines_2005-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_2002_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_2002-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> respectively. The former poll was an attempt to determine the world's favourite song, while the Guinness poll took place in the UK. Both songs have been inducted into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Hall_of_Fame" title="Grammy Hall of Fame">Grammy Hall of Fame</a>; "Bohemian Rhapsody" in 2004 and "We Are the Champions" in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2007 the video for "Bohemian Rhapsody" was voted the greatest of all time by readers of <a href="/wiki/Q_(magazine)" title="Q (magazine)"><i>Q</i> magazine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-video_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-video-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Consistently rated as one of the greatest singers in the history of popular music, Mercury was voted second to <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> in MTV's 22 Greatest Voices in Music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fitzpatrick_2006_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzpatrick_2006-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, in January 2009, Mercury was voted second to <a href="/wiki/Robert_Plant" title="Robert Plant">Robert Plant</a> in a poll of the greatest voices in rock, on the digital radio station <a href="/wiki/Planet_Rock_(radio_station)" title="Planet Rock (radio station)">Planet Rock</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> In May 2009 a <i><a href="/wiki/Classic_Rock_(magazine)" title="Classic Rock (magazine)">Classic Rock</a></i> magazine poll saw Mercury voted the greatest singer in rock.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011 <a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a> magazine readers voted Mercury second to <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> in the Greatest Singers Ever poll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011 a <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> readers' pick placed Mercury in second place of the magazine's "Best Lead Singers of All Time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSBestSingers_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-RSBestSingers-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013 <a href="/wiki/Gigwise" title="Gigwise">Gigwise</a> readers named Mercury the best frontman ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Posthumous_Queen_album">Posthumous <i>Queen</i> album</span></h3>
<p>In November 1995 Queen released <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Made_in_Heaven_(album)" title="Made in Heaven (album)">Made in Heaven</a></i>, an album featuring Freddie Mercury's previously unreleased final recordings from 1991—as well as outtakes from previous years and reworked versions of solo works by the surviving members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heaven_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heaven-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The album cover features the Freddie Mercury statue that overlooks Lake Geneva in <a href="/wiki/Montreux" title="Montreux">Montreux</a>, Switzerland, where he had written and recorded his last songs at <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Studios" title="Mountain Studios">Mountain Studios</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heaven_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-Heaven-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The sleeve of the album contains the words, "Dedicated to the immortal spirit of Freddie Mercury."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heaven_124-2"><a href="#cite_note-Heaven-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tributes">Tributes</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:167px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Freddy_Mercury_Statue_Montreux.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3003" data-file-width="1551" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Freddy_Mercury_Statue_Montreux.jpg/165px-Freddy_Mercury_Statue_Montreux.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Freddy_Mercury_Statue_Montreux.jpg/248px-Freddy_Mercury_Statue_Montreux.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Freddy_Mercury_Statue_Montreux.jpg/330px-Freddy_Mercury_Statue_Montreux.jpg 2x" width="165"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Freddy_Mercury_Statue_Montreux.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of Freddie Mercury overlooking <a href="/wiki/Lake_Geneva" title="Lake Geneva">Lake Geneva</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montreux" title="Montreux">Montreux</a>, Switzerland.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A statue in Montreux, Switzerland (by sculptor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irena_Sedlecka" title="Irena Sedlecka">Irena Sedlecka</a>) was erected as a tribute to Mercury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> It stands almost 10 feet (3 metres) high overlooking Lake Geneva and was unveiled on 25 November 1996 by Mercury's father and Montserrat Caballé, with bandmates Brian May and Roger Taylor also in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Beginning in 2003 fans from around the world have gathered in Switzerland annually to pay tribute to the singer as part of the "Freddie Mercury Montreux Memorial Day" on the first weekend of September. The Bearpark And Esh Colliery Band played at the Freddie Mercury statue on 1 June 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bishton_2004_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bishton_2004-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1997 the three remaining members of Queen released "<a href="/wiki/No-One_but_You_(Only_the_Good_Die_Young)" title="No-One but You (Only the Good Die Young)">No-One but You (Only the Good Die Young)</a>," a song dedicated to Mercury and all those that die too soon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1999 a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Mail" title="Royal Mail">Royal Mail</a> stamp with an image of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millennium_Stamp#Great_Britain" title="Millennium Stamp">Mercury on stage</a> was issued in his honour as part of the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_stamp#1999" title="Millennium stamp">Millennium Stamp</a> series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:187px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="412" data-file-width="284" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1a/WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg/185px-WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1a/WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg/278px-WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/1a/WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg 2x" width="185"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WeWillRockYouDominion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mercury statue above the West End's <a href="/wiki/Dominion_Theatre" title="Dominion Theatre">Dominion Theatre</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2009 a plaque was unveiled in <a href="/wiki/Feltham" title="Feltham">Feltham</a>, where Mercury and his family moved upon arriving in England in 1964. The star in memory of Mercury's achievements was unveiled on Feltham High Street by his mother Jer Bulsara and Queen bandmate Brian May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> A tribute to Queen was on display at the <a href="/wiki/Fremont_Street_Experience" title="Fremont Street Experience">Fremont Street Experience</a> in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Las_Vegas" title="Downtown Las Vegas">downtown Las Vegas</a> throughout 2009 on its video canopy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2009 a large model of Mercury wearing <a href="/wiki/Tartan" title="Tartan">tartan</a> was put on display in the centre of Edinburgh as publicity for the run of <i>We Will Rock You</i> at the Playhouse Theatre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A statue of Mercury stands over the entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_Theatre" title="Dominion Theatre">Dominion Theatre</a> in London's West End since May 2002, where the main show has been Queen and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Elton" title="Ben Elton">Ben Elton</a>'s musical <i><a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You_(musical)" title="We Will Rock You (musical)">We Will Rock You</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>For Mercury's 65th birthday <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> dedicated their <a href="/wiki/Google_Doodle" title="Google Doodle">Google Doodle</a> to him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> It included an animation set to the Mercury penned song, "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Stop_Me_Now" title="Don't Stop Me Now">Don't Stop Me Now</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
