<p>Referring to "the late, great Freddie Mercury" in their 2012 <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> induction speech, <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a> quoted Mercury's lyrics from his song "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_the_Champions" title="We Are the Champions">We Are the Champions</a>"; "I’ve taken my bows, my curtain calls, you’ve brought me fame and fortune and everything that goes with it, and I thank you all."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Tribute was paid to Queen and Mercury at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_closing_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics closing ceremony">closing ceremony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> in London. The band's performance of "<a href="/wiki/We_Will_Rock_You" title="We Will Rock You">We Will Rock You</a>" with solo artist <a href="/wiki/Jessie_J" title="Jessie J">Jessie J</a> was opened with a remastered video of Mercury's "call and response" routine from 1986's Wembley Stadium performance, with the 2012 crowd at the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(London)" title="Olympic Stadium (London)">Olympic Stadium</a> responding appropriately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Importance_in_AIDS_history">Importance in AIDS history</span></h3>
<p>As the first major rock star to die of AIDS, Mercury's death represented a very important event in the history of the disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> In April 1992 the remaining members of Queen founded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Mercury_Phoenix_Trust" title="The Mercury Phoenix Trust">The Mercury Phoenix Trust</a> and organised <i><a href="/wiki/The_Freddie_Mercury_Tribute_Concert" title="The Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert">The Freddie Mercury Tribute Concert for AIDS Awareness</a></i>, to celebrate the life and legacy of Mercury and raise money for AIDS research, which took place on 20 April 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stothard_1992_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stothard_1992-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> The Mercury Phoenix Trust has since raised millions of pounds for various AIDS charities. The tribute concert, which took place at London's <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a> for an audience of 72,000, featured a wide variety of guests including <a href="/wiki/Robert_Plant" title="Robert Plant">Robert Plant</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>), <a href="/wiki/Roger_Daltrey" title="Roger Daltrey">Roger Daltrey</a> (of <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">The Who</a>), <a href="/wiki/Extreme_(band)" title="Extreme (band)">Extreme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annie_Lennox" title="Annie Lennox">Annie Lennox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Iommi" title="Tony Iommi">Tony Iommi</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a>), <a href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses" title="Guns N' Roses">Guns N' Roses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Taylor" title="Elizabeth Taylor">Elizabeth Taylor</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Def_Leppard" title="Def Leppard">Def Leppard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seal_(musician)" title="Seal (musician)">Seal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liza_Minnelli" title="Liza Minnelli">Liza Minnelli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> (via satellite). Elizabeth Taylor spoke of Mercury as "an extraordinary rock star who rushed across our cultural landscape like a comet shooting across the sky."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> The concert was broadcast live to 76 countries and had an estimated viewing audience of 1 billion people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC_2007_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_2007-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearances_in_lists_of_influential_individuals">Appearances in lists of influential individuals</span></h3>
<p>Several popularity polls conducted over the past decade indicate that Freddie Mercury's reputation may, in fact, have been enhanced since his death. For instance, in a 2002 vote to determine who the UK public considers the greatest British people in history, Mercury was ranked 58 in the list of the "<a href="/wiki/100_Greatest_Britons" title="100 Greatest Britons">100 Greatest Britons</a>," broadcast by the BBC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> He was further listed at the 52nd spot in a 2007 Japanese national survey of the 100 most "influential heroes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-James_2007_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-James_2007-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite the fact that he had been criticised by gay activists for hiding his HIV status, author Paul Russell included Mercury in his book "The Gay 100: A Ranking of the Most Influential Gay Men and Lesbians, Past and Present."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russell_2002_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-Russell_2002-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Other entertainers on Russell's list included <a href="/wiki/Liberace" title="Liberace">Liberace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rock_Hudson" title="Rock Hudson">Rock Hudson</a>. In 2008 <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine ranked Mercury 18 on its list of the "Top 100 Singers Of All Time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rollingstone.com_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-rollingstone.com-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portrayal_on_stage">Portrayal on stage</span></h3>
<p>On 24 November 1997, a <a href="/wiki/Monodrama" title="Monodrama">monodrama</a> about Freddie Mercury's life, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Mercury:_The_Afterlife_and_Times_of_a_Rock_God" title="Mercury: The Afterlife and Times of a Rock God">Mercury: The Afterlife and Times of a Rock God</a></i>, opened in New York City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> It presented Freddie Mercury in the hereafter: examining his life, seeking redemption and searching for his true self.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> The play was written and directed by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Messina" title="Charles Messina">Charles Messina</a> and the part of Mercury was played by <a href="/wiki/Khalid_Gon%C3%A7alves" title="Khalid Gonçalves">Khalid Gonçalves</a> (né Paul Gonçalves) and then later, <a href="/wiki/Amir_Darvish" title="Amir Darvish">Amir Darvish</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Billy_Squier" title="Billy Squier">Billy Squier</a> opened one of the shows with an acoustic performance of a song he had written about Mercury titled "I Have Watched You Fly."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portrayals_in_film_and_television">Portrayals in film and television</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_film">Proposed film <span id="biopic"></span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a> announced in a September 2010 BBC interview<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> that <a href="/wiki/Sacha_Baron_Cohen" title="Sacha Baron Cohen">Sacha Baron Cohen</a>, previously known for his comedic characters <a href="/wiki/Borat_Sagdiyev" title="Borat Sagdiyev">Borat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ali_G" title="Ali G">Ali G</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCno_(character)" title="Brüno (character)">Brüno</a>, had been chosen to play Mercury in a film about his life. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_magazine" title="Time magazine">TIME</a></i> commented with approval on his singing ability and resemblance to Mercury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> The motion picture is being written by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Morgan" title="Peter Morgan">Peter Morgan</a>, who had been nominated for Oscars for his screenplays <i><a href="/wiki/The_Queen_(film)" title="The Queen (film)">The Queen</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Frost/Nixon_(film)" title="Frost/Nixon (film)">Frost/Nixon</a></i>. The film, which is being co-produced by <a href="/wiki/Robert_De_Niro" title="Robert De Niro">Robert De Niro</a>'s <a href="/wiki/TriBeCa_Productions" title="TriBeCa Productions">TriBeCa Productions</a>, will focus on Queen's formative years and the period leading up to the celebrated performance at the <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">1985 Live Aid</a> concert. Filming was planned to begin sometime in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2011 Brian May confirmed that a lot of work was still being done in preparation for the film. He said that after holding back for a long time due to mixed feelings, the band had approved a team to start filming later in 2011, and Baron Cohen's eagerness had been the key to progress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> However, in July 2013, it was reported that Baron Cohen dropped out of the role due to "creative differences" between him and the surviving band members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Later, Queen guitarist Brian May said they split on good terms and gave the reason for the split that they felt Cohen's presence would be "distracting."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2013 it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Ben_Whishaw" title="Ben Whishaw">Ben Whishaw</a>, best known for playing <a href="/wiki/Q_(James_Bond)" title="Q (James Bond)">Q</a> in the <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_film" title="James Bond in film">James Bond film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Skyfall" title="Skyfall">Skyfall</a></i>, had been chosen to replace Cohen in the role of Mercury.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whishaw_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-whishaw-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also announced that British actor and director <a href="/wiki/Dexter_Fletcher" title="Dexter Fletcher">Dexter Fletcher</a> would direct the film, however Fletcher subsequently withdrew from the project in March 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fletcher_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-fletcher-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> Prior to Fletcher's withdrawal, production on the film had been due to begin in the summer of 2014; any delays would cause further problems, with Whishaw already committed to begin work on the next James Bond film towards the end of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fletcher_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-fletcher-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_portrayals">Other portrayals</span></h4>
<p>Mercury appeared as a supporting character in the BBC television drama <i>Best Possible Taste: The <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Everett" title="Kenny Everett">Kenny Everett</a> Story</i>, first broadcast in October 2012. He was portrayed by actor <a href="/wiki/James_Floyd_(actor)" title="James Floyd (actor)">James Floyd</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frog_genus">Frog genus</span></h3>
<p>A novel genus of frogs <i><a href="/wiki/Mercurana" title="Mercurana">Mercurana</a></i>, discovered in 2013 from <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>, India, was named as a tribute because Mercury's "vibrant music inspires the authors." In addition, the site of discovery is very near to where Mercury spent most of his childhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robin_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-robin-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<dl>
<dd>a.<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Parsisnone"><a href="#ref_Parsisnone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> On Mercury's birth certificate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LindaB_2000_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-LindaB_2000-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> his parents defined themselves with "Nationality: British Indian" and "Race: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parsi_people" title="Parsi people">Parsi</a>". The Parsis are an originally <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" title="Persian people">Persian</a> ethnic group of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> who follow <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>.</dd>
<dd>b.<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Bulsaranone"><a href="#ref_Bulsaranone"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> The Bulsara family gets its name from Bulsar, a city and district that is now in the Indian state of <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> and is today officially known as <a href="/wiki/Valsad" title="Valsad">Valsad</a>. In the 17th century, Bulsar was one of the five centres of the <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrian</a> religion (the other four were also in what is today Gujarat) and consequently "Bulsara" is a relatively common name amongst Zoroastrians.</dd>
</dl>

"Two novel genera and one new species of treefrog (Anura: Rhacophoridae) highlight cryptic diversity in the Western Ghats of India". <i>Zootaxa</i> <b>3640</b> (2): 177–189. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.11646%2Fzootaxa.3640.2.3" rel="nofollow">10.11646/zootaxa.3640.2.3</a>.</span><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AFreddie+Mercury&amp;rft.atitle=Two+novel+genera+and+one+new+species+of+treefrog+%28Anura%3A+Rhacophoridae%29+highlight+cryptic+diversity+in+the+Western+Ghats+of+India&amp;rft.aulast=Robin+Kurian+Abraham%2C+R.+Alexander+Pyron%2C+Ansil+B.+R.%2C+Arun+Zachariah%2C+Anil+Zachariah&amp;rft.au=Robin+Kurian+Abraham%2C+R.+Alexander+Pyron%2C+Ansil+B.+R.%2C+Arun+Zachariah%2C+Anil+Zachariah&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.11646%2Fzootaxa.3640.2.3&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.jtitle=Zootaxa&amp;rft.pages=177-189&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=3640"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<p><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Highest_Notes"><b><a href="#ref_Highest_Notes">^</a></b></span> Notation done in <a href="/wiki/Scientific_pitch_notation" title="Scientific pitch notation">scientific pitch</a>, and thus is written one octave lower than what is displayed here.</p>
